Part IV
The Judiciary
The High Court of the Cook Islands
[Part IV : replaced, on 5 June 1981, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 9) Act 1980–81
(1980–81 No 24).]
47 High Court established
(1) There shall be a Court of record, to be called the High Court of the Cook
Islands, for the administration of justice throughout those islands.
(2) Except as provided in this Constitution or by law , the High Court shall have all
such jurisdiction (both civil jurisdiction, including jurisdiction in relation to
land, and criminal jurisdiction) as may be necessary to administer the law in
force in the Cook Islands.
(3) There shall be 3 Divisions of the High Court, namely—
(a) a Civil Division:
(b) a Criminal Division:
(c) a Land Division.
(4) A Judge of the High Court may exercise any of the jurisdiction and powers of
a Judge of any Division.
(5) Nothing in this Article shall prevent a Judge of any Division from exercising
any of the powers of a Judge of the High Court, whether or not in his capacity
as a Judge of that Division.
(6) Subject to the foregoing provisions of this Article and to Article 48 hereof, each
Judge of the High Court, or any 2 or more Judges, may , in any part of the Cook
Islands and at any time or place, exercise all the powers of the High Court.
48 Jurisdiction of Divisions of the High Court
(1) Each Division of the High Court shall hear and determine—
(a) such proceedings as are, under or by virtue of any enactment, to be heard
and determined by that Division:
(b) such other proceedings as may from time to time be determined by the
Chief Justice, either generally or in any particular proceedings or classes
of proceedings.
(2) Subject to subclause (3) of this Article, the Land Division shall have all the
jurisdiction and powers in relation to land that immediately before the
commencement of this Article were conferred on the Land Court of the Cook
Islands, and shall have such other jurisdiction as may be conferred on it by
enactment.
(3) Notwithstanding anything in this Part or Part IV A, and in recognition of the
customs and traditions of the people of those islands, the Land Division shall not
exercise any jurisdiction or power in relation to land or chieﬂy titles in any of
the islands of Mangaia, Mitiaro and Pukapuka, and such other islands as may be
prescribed by Act, provided that no such Act shall be introduced to Parliament
except with the consent of the Aronga Mana of the island to which it relates.
(4) Where on any island to which subclause (3) applies, jurisdiction or power in
relation to land or chieﬂy titles is exercised in accordance with the customs and
Service 0115,901

usages of that island, the exercise of that jurisdiction of power shall be ﬁnal and
binding on all persons af fected thereby , and shall not be questioned in any court
of law .
(5) The High Court may exercise its jurisdiction at any place within or outside of
the Cook Islands and on such dates and at such times as the Chief Justice may
from time to time determine.
[Article 48(3): replaced, on 1 July 1995, by section 5 of the Constitution Amendment (No 17) Act
1994–95 (1994–95 No 36).]
[Article 48(4): inserted, on 1 July 1995, by section 5 of the Constitution Amendment (No 17) Act
1994–95 (1994–95 No 36).]
[Article 48(5): inserted, on 26 November 2009, by section 2 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
49 Judges of the High Court
(1) The High Court shall consist of 1 or more Judges, each of whom shall be
appointed under the provisions of this Constitution.
(2) If only 1 Judge is so appointed, he shall be the Chief Justice of the Cook Islands,
but if more than 1 Judge is appointed, one of them shall be appointed as the
Chief Justice of the Cook Islands.
(3) A person shall not be qualiﬁed for appointment as a Judge of the High Court
under this Article, unless—
(a) he holds or has held of f ice as a Judge of the High Court of New Zealand
or the New Zealand Maori Land Court or an equivalent of f ice in any part
of the Commonwealth or in a designated country; or
(b) he has been in practice as a barrister or solicitor for a period, or periods,
amounting in the aggregate to not less than 7 years in one or more of
either,—
(i) Cook Islands:
(ii) New Zealand:
(iii) a part of the Commonwealth:
(iv) a designated country .
(4) The Queen’s Representative, acting in his discretion, may declare to be a
designated country for the purposes of this Article any country which in his
opinion has a legal system similar to that existing in New Zealand.
(5) Judges of the High Court, other than the Chief Justice, shall take seniority
according to the respective dates of their appointment as judges, whether of the
High Court or the Court of Appeal or of the High Court of New Zealand or of
any superior court in any place outside the Cook Islands or New Zealand.
[Article 49(3)(a): replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 3(1) of the Constitution Amendment
(No 28) Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
[Article 49(3)(b): replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 3(1) of the Constitution Amendment
(No 28) Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
[Article 49(4): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Article 49(5): inserted, on 26 November 2009, by section 3(2) of the Constitution Amendment (No
28) Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
50 Acting Chief Justice of the High Court
Where any vacancy exists in the of f ice of Chief Justice of the High Court or the
Chief Justice of the High Court is absent from the Cook Islands, or is, by reason
of illness or any cause other than absence from the Cook Islands, unable to
Art 48LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 115,902

perform the of f ice or exercise any function of Chief Justice of the High Court,
the senior other Judge of the High Court for the time being in the Cook Islands
may perform that of f ice or exercise that function until a Chief Justice of the
High Court is appointed, or, as the case may be the Chief Justice of the High
Court resumes that of f ice or exercises that function.
51 Acting Judge of the High Court
(1) The Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Chief Justice and the
Attorney General, may appoint any person who is qualiﬁed for appointment as
a Judge of the High Court to act as a Judge of the High Court, if there is no
Judge of the High Court for the time being in the Cook Islands or, by reason of
illness or other cause, there is no Judge of the High Court available to act.
(2) Any appointment made under this Article may be revoked at any time by the
Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Chief Justice.
[Article 51(1): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20); on 26 November 2009, by section 4 of the
Constitution Amendment (No 28) Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
[Article 51(2): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
Appointment, T enure of Of fıce and Salaries of Judges
52 Appointment of Judges
The Chief Justice and other Judges of the High Court shall be appointed as
follows:
(a) the Chief Justice of the High Court shall be appointed by the Queen’s
Representative, acting on the advice of the Executive Council tendered
by the Prime Minister:
(b) the other Judges of the High Court shall be appointed by the Queen’s
Representative acting on the recommendation of the Executive Council
made on the advice of the Chief Justice and the Attorney General.
[Article 52(a): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Article 52(b): replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 5 of the Constitution Amendment (No
28) Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
53 T enure of of fice of Judges
(1) Except in the case of an appointment made under subclause (2) of this Article,
no person who has attained the age of 70 years shall be appointed to or continue
to hold of f ice as the Chief Justice or other Judge of the High Court.
(2) Any person of any age who does not reside in the Cook Islands and who is
qualiﬁed for appointment may be appointed to hold of f ice as the Chief Justice or
other Judge of the High Court for a term of not more than 3 years, but may be
reappointed for one or more further terms, being in each case a term of not more
than 3 years.
(3) Nothing done by the Chief Justice or other Judge of the High Court in the
performance of his functions shall be deemed to be invalid by reason only that
he has reached the age at which he is required by this Article to retire or that his
term has expired, as the case may be.
Art 53 CONSTITUTION OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0115,903

(4) The Chief Justice or any other Judge of the High Court may resign his of f ice by
writing under his hand addressed to the Queen’s Representative.
[Article 53(4): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
54 Removal of Judge from of fice
(1) The Chief Justice or any other Judge of the High Court, other than a Judge
appointed under the provisions of Article 51 hereof, may be removed from of f ice
by the Queen’s Representative only for inability to discharge the functions of his
of f ice (whether arising from inﬁrmity of body or mind or from any other cause)
or misbehaviour, and shall not be so removed unless the question of removal of
the Chief Justice or other Judge from of f ice has been referred to a tribunal
appointed under subclause (2) of this Article and that tribunal has recommended
that the Chief Justice or other Judge be removed from of f ice for inability as
aforesaid or misbehaviour.
(2) If the Prime Minister advises the Queen’s Representative that the question of
removing from of f ice the Chief Justice or any other Judge of the High Court for
inability as aforesaid or misbehaviour ought to be investigated, then—
(a) the Queen’s Representative shall appoint a tribunal consisting of a
chairman and 2 other members; and
(b) the tribunal shall inquire into the matter and report on the facts thereof to
the Queen’s Representative and recommend to the Queen’s
Representative whether or not the Chief Justice or other Judges should be
removed from of f ice; and
(c) if the tribunal recommends that the Chief Justice or other Judge be so
removed, the Queen’s Representative shall, by warrant, revoke the
appointment of the Chief Justice or other Judge, as the case may be.
(3) No person shall be qualiﬁed for appointment as a member of a tribunal under
this Article unless he is qualiﬁed for appointment as a Judge of the High Court
under Article 49 hereof.
(4) No business shall be transacted by a tribunal appointed under this Article unless
all 3 members are present, and all questions proposed for decision by the
tribunal shall be decided by the votes of a majority of those members.
(5) Subject to this Article, the tribunal shall determine its own procedure.
(6) If the question of removing from of f ice the Chief Justice or any other Judge of
the High Court has been referred to a tribunal under subclause (2) of this
Article—
(a) the Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Prime Minister,
may suspend the Chief Justice or other Judge from performing the
functions of his of f ice for a period of 1 month:
(b) if the decision of the tribunal has not been given before the expiration of
that period, the Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the
Executive Council tendered to him by the Prime Minister, may suspend
the Chief Justice or other Judge from performing the functions of his
of f ice for a further period of 1 month.
(7) Any such suspension may be at any time revoked by the Queen’s
Representative, acting on the advice of the Prime Minister in the case of a
suspension under paragraph (a) of subclause (6) of this Article and on the advice
of the Executive Council in the case of a suspension under paragraph (b) of that
subclause, and shall in any case cease to have ef fect if the tribunal—
Art 53LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 115,904

(a) before the expiration of the total period of suspension, recommends to the
Queen’s Representative that the Chief Justice or other Judge be not
removed from of f ice; or
(b) does not, before the expiration of the total period of suspension,
recommend to the Queen’s Representative that the Chief Justice or other
Judge be removed from of f ice.
[Article 54: amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution Amendment
(No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
55 Salaries of Judges
(1) The salaries of the Chief Justice and other Judges of the High Court shall be
determined by Act, and shall be charged on the Cook Islands Government
Account.
(2) The salaries of those Judges shall not be diminished during their period of of f ice,
unless as part of a general reduction of salaries applied proportionately to all
persons whose salaries are determined by enactment.
55A Masters of the High Court
(1) The Chief Justice may , after consultation with the Solicitor General and a senior
practitioner appointed by the Law Society for the purpose, appoint Masters of
the High Court.
(2) An enactment shall prescribe—
(a) the qualiﬁcations of persons to be appointed Masters:
(b) the manner in which Masters are appointed:
(c) the terms and conditions of their appointment:
(d) the jurisdiction and powers to be exercised by a Master; and
(e) conditions for the review of, or appeals against, decisions of Masters by
a Judge of the High Court.
[Article 55A: inserted, on 26 November 2009, by section 6 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
Court of Appeal
[Heading: inserted, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28) Act
2009 (2009 No 17).]
56 Court of Appeal
(1) There shall be a Court of Appeal of the Cook Islands, which shall be a superior
Court of record.
(2) Subject to Articles 57 and 58, the Judges of the Court of Appeal shall be—
(a) the Chief Justice and other Judges of the High Court; and
(b) such other persons, possessing the qualiﬁcations prescribed by subclause
(3) of this Article, as may from time to time be appointed by the Queen’s
Representative acting on the recommendation of the Executive Council
made on the advice of the Chief Justice and the Attorney General.
(3) No person shall be qualiﬁed for appointment as a Judge of the Court of Appeal
under paragraph (b) of subclause (2) of this Article, unless that person is
qualiﬁed under Article 49 to be appointed as a Judge of the High Court.
(4) A Judge of the Court of Appeal appointed under subclause (2)(b) of this Article
shall be appointed President of the Court of Appeal by the Queen’s
Art 56 CONSTITUTION OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0115,905

Representative acting upon the recommendation of the Executive Council made
on the advice of the Chief Justice and the Attorney General.
(5) The Chief Justice, if present, shall preside at a sitting of the Court of Appeal but
otherwise, the President shall preside or in his absence, the senior Judge.
(6) Judges of the Court of Appeal shall take seniority according to the respective
dates of their ﬁrst appointment as Judges, whether of the High Court or of the
Court of Appeal or of the High Court of New Zealand or of any superior court
in any place outside the Cook Islands or New Zealand.
[Article 56: replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
57 Number of Judges
(1) Any 3 Judges of the Court of Appeal may exercise all the powers of the Court.
(2) The judgment of the Court of Appeal shall be in accordance with the opinion of
the majority of the Judges present.
(3) Notwithstanding subclause (1) of this Article, an Act may prescribe powers of
the Court that may be exercised by the President, a Judge of the Court of Appeal
or the Registrar on its behalf.
[Article 57: replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
58 Judges not to sit on appeals from own decision
Judge of the Court of Appeal shall not sit on the hearing of an appeal from any
decision made by him or by a Court on which he sat as a member.
[Article 58: replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
59 Hearings and determination of Court of Appeal
(1) The Court of Appeal may exercise its jurisdiction at any place within or outside
of the Cook Islands and on such dates and at such times as the President, after
consultation with the Chief Justice, may from time to time determine.
(2) Except as provided in subclause (3) of this Article, the determination of the
Court of Appeal shall be ﬁnal.
(3) There shall be a right of appeal to Her Majesty the Queen in Council, with the
leave of the Court of Appeal, or, if such leave is refused, with the leave of Her
Majesty the Queen in Council, from judgments of the Court of Appeal in such
cases and subject to such conditions as are prescribed by Act.
[Article 59: replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
60 Jurisdiction of Court of Appeal
(1) Subject to the provisions of this Constitution, and as may be prescribed by Act,
the Court of Appeal shall have jurisdiction to hear and determine,—
(a) any appeal from a judgment of the High Court; and
(b) any cause or matter removed by the High Court to the Court of Appeal.
(2) Notwithstanding anything in subclause (1) of this Article, and any limitations as
may be prescribed by Act, the Court of Appeal may in any case in which it
thinks ﬁt and at any time, grant special leave to appeal to that Court from any
judgment of the High Court, subject to such conditions as to security for costs
and otherwise as the Court of Appeal thinks ﬁt.
Art 56LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 115,906

(3) In this Article the term judgment includes any judgment, decree, order, writ,
declaration, conviction, sentence, or other determination.
[Article 60: replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
61 T ransmission of order of Court of Appeal
The determination of the Court of Appeal on any appeal from the High Court
shall be transmitted to the Registrar of the High Court by the Registrar of the
Court of Appeal under the seal of the Court of Appeal, and judgment shall
thereupon be entered by the High Court in conformity with that determination,
or such other proceedings by way of a new trial or otherwise shall be taken in
the High Court as are required by that determination.
[Article 61: replaced, on 26 November 2009, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 28)
Act 2009 (2009 No 17).]
Justices of the Peace
62 Justices of the Peace
(1) The Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Executive Council
tendered to him by the Minister of Justice, may appoint Justices of the Peace for
the Cook Islands, who shall hold of f ice for such time as may be prescribed in
their warrants of appointment and may be paid such remuneration as may be
prescribed by enactment.
(2) Every Justice of the Peace (whether appointed before or after the coming into
force of this subclause) shall cease to act in a judicial capacity before becoming
a candidate for election to Parliament, but such ceasing to act shall not otherwise
af fect that person’s status as a Justice of the Peace.
(3) An Act shall prescribe the jurisdiction and powers of Justices of the Peace
appointed under this Article and for an appeal to lie to the High Court from a
ﬁnal judgment of a Justice of the Peace.
(4) A Justice of the Peace for the Cook Islands shall not be removed from of f ice as
such, except by the Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Chief
Justice.
(5) In subclause (3) of this Article the term judgment includes any judgment,
decree, order, writ, declaration, conviction, sentence, or other determination.

Oath of Allegiance and Judicial Oath
63 Oath of Allegiance and Judicial Oath
(1) Every Judge of the Court of Appeal who is not a Judge of the Court of Appeal
of New Zealand or of the High Court of New Zealand or a Judge of the High
Court of the Cook Islands and every Justice of the Peace for the Cook Islands,
Art 63 CONSTITUTION OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0115,907

shall, as soon as may be after his acceptance of of f ice, take and subscribe before
the Queen’s Representative the following oaths—
(a) An Oath of Allegiance in the following form:
I, . . . . . . . . . . . . . . ., swear by Almighty God that I will be faithful and
bear true allegiance to Her [ or His] Majesty [ Specify the name of the
reigning Sovereign as thus : Queen Elizabeth the Second] as the Head of
State of the Cook Islands, Her [ or His] heirs, and successors, in
accordance with the Constitution and the law . So help me God.
(b) The Judicial Oath in the following form:
I, . . . . . . . . . . . . . . ., swear by Almighty God that I will well and truly
serve Her [or His] Majesty [Specify as above] as the Head of State of the
Cook Islands, Her [ or His] heirs, and successors, in accordance with the
Constitution and the law , in the of f ice of . . . . . . . . . . . . . .; and I will do
right to all manner of people, without fear or favour, af fection or ill will.
So help me God.
(2) If any person mentioned in this Article declines or neglects, when the oaths
required to be taken by him under this Article are duly tendered, to take those
oaths, he shall if he has already entered on his of f ice vacate the same, and if he
has not entered on the same be disqualiﬁed from entering on the same; but no
person shall be compelled in respect of the same appointment to the same of f ice
to take any oath more than once:
Provided that no proceedings before any such person may be questioned in any
Court solely on the ground that that person has failed to take the oaths
prescribed by this Article.
[Article 63(1): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]

Part IV A
Fundamental human rights and freedoms
[Part IV A: inserted, on 5 June 1981, by section 8 of the Constitution Amendment (No 9) Act
1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
64 Fundamental human rights and freedoms
(1) It is hereby recognised and declared that in the Cook Islands there exist, and
shall continue to exist, without discrimination by reason of race, national origin,
colour, religion, opinion, belief, or sex, the following fundamental human rights
and freedoms—
(a) the right of the individual to life, liberty , and security of the person, and
the right not to be deprived thereof except in accordance with law:
(b) the right of the individual to equality before the law and to the protection
of the law:
(c) the right of the individual to own property and the right not to be
deprived thereof except in accordance with law:
Provided that nothing in this paragraph or in Article 40 of this
Constitution shall be construed as limiting the power of Parliament to
prohibit or restrict by Act the alienation of Native land (as deﬁned in
section 2(1) of the Cook Islands Act 1915 of the Parliament of New
Zealand):
(d) freedom of thought, conscience, and religion:
(e) freedom of speech and expression:
(f) freedom of peaceful assembly and association.
(2) It is hereby recognised and declared that every person has duties to others, and
accordingly is subject in the exercise of his rights and freedoms to such
limitations as are imposed, by any enactment or rule of law for the time being
in force, for protecting the rights and freedoms of others or in the interests of
public safety , order, or morals, the general welfare, or the security of the Cook
Islands.
65 Construction of law
(1) Subject to subclause (2) of this Article and to subclause (2) of Article 64 hereof,
every enactment shall be so construed and applied as not to abrogate, abridge,
or infringe or to authorise the abrogation, abridgement, or infringement of any
of the rights or freedoms recognised and declared by subclause (1) of Article 64
hereof, and in particular no enactment shall be construed or applied so as to—
(a) authorise or ef fect the arbitrary detention, imprisonment, or exile of any
person; or
(b) impose or authorise the imposition on any person of cruel and unusual
treatment or punishment; or
(c) deprive any person who is arrested or detained—
(i) of the right to be informed promptly of the act or omission for
which he is arrested or detained, unless it is impracticable to do so
or unless the reason for the arrest or detention is obvious in the
circumstances; or
(ii) of the right, wherever practicable to retain and instruct a barrister
or solicitor without delay; or
Service 0116,101

(iii) of the right to apply , by himself or by any other person on his
behalf, for a writ of habeas corpus for the determination of the
validity of his detention, and to be released if his detention is not
lawful; or
(d) deprive any person of the right to a fair hearing, in accordance with the
principles of fundamental justice, for the determination of his rights and
obligations before any tribunal or authority having a duty to act
judicially; or
(e) deprive any person charged with an of fence of the right to be presumed
innocent until he is proved guilty according to law in a fair and public
hearing by an independent and impartial tribunal; or
(f) deprive any person charged with an of fence of the right to reasonable
bail, except for just cause; or
(g) authorise the conviction of any person of any of fence except for the
breach of a law in force at the time of the act or omission; or
(h) authorise the imposition on any person convicted of any of fence of a
penalty heavier than that which might have been imposed under the law
in force at the time of the commission of the of fence.
(2) Every enactment, and every provision thereof shall be deemed remedial,
whether its immediate purpose is to direct the doing of anything, that the
enacting authority deems to be for the public good, or to prevent or punish the
doing of anything it deems contrary to the public good, and shall accordingly
receive such fair, large, and liberal construction and interpretation as will best
ensure the attainment of the object of the enactment or provision thereof
according to its true intent, meaning and spirit.
(3) In this Article the term enactment includes any Act of the Parliament of
England or the Parliament of Great Britain or the Parliament of the United
Kingdom, being an Act in force in the Cook Islands, and any regulation, rule,
order, or other instrument made thereunder.
[Article 65(2): amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 9 of the Constitution Amendment (No 10) Act
1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
66 Saving
Nothing in this Part of this Constitution shall limit or af fect any right or
freedom, not speciﬁed in this Part, that may exist in the Cook Islands at the
commencement of this Part.
[The next page is 116,301]
Art 65LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 116,102

Part IVB
Custom
[Part IVB: inserted, on 1 July 1995, by section 7 of the Constitution Amendment (No 17) Act
1994–95 (1994–95 No 36).]
66A Custom
(1) In addition to its power to make laws pursuant to Article 39, Parliament may
make laws recognising or giving ef fect to custom and usage.
(2) In exercising its powers pursuant to this Article, Parliament shall have particular
regard to the customs, traditions, usages, and values of the indigenous people of
the Cook Islands.
(3) Until such time as an Act otherwise provides, custom and usage shall have ef fect
as part of the law of the Cook Islands, provided that this subclause shall not
apply in respect of any custom, tradition, usage or value that is, and to the extent
that it is, inconsistent with a provision of this Constitution or of any enactment.
(4) For the purposes of this Constitution, the opinion or decision of the Aronga
Mana of the island or vaka to which a custom, tradition, usage or value relates,
as to matters relating to and concerning custom, tradition, usage or the
existence, extent or application of custom shall be ﬁnal and conclusive and shall
not be questioned in any court of law .
Service 0116,301

[The next page is 116,501]
LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 116,302

Part V
The Public revenues of the Cook Islands
67 Public funds
There shall be a Cook Islands Government Account and such other public funds
or accounts as may be provided by law .
68 Restriction on taxation
No taxation shall be imposed except by law .
69 Public revenue
All taxes and other revenues and money raised or received by the Government
of the Cook Islands shall be paid into the Cook Islands Government Account
unless required or permitted by law to be paid into any other public fund or
account.
70 Expenditure
(1) All expenditure from the Cook Islands Government Account, or from any other
public fund or account shall be in accordance with an Appropriation Act unless
otherwise authorised or permitted by any other enactment.
(2) An appropriation provision for a speciﬁc purpose shall make reference to any
anticipated income in relation to that purpose and the amount appropriated shall
be the net amount.
(3) The Minister responsible for Finance, with the concurrence of Cabinet, or,
where any enactment so provides, the Executive Council, may approve the
expenditure of such sums as he or it considers necessary—
(a) in anticipation of provision to be made in an Appropriation Act for any
ﬁnancial year:
Provided that the total amount issued and paid in any ﬁnancial year shall
not exceed the unexpended balance of the vote in the Appropriation Act
(or Acts) for the preceding ﬁnancial year together with an amount equal
to three-twelfths of that vote; or
(b) when during the period between the passing of the last Appropriation Act
for any ﬁnancial year and the end of that year it is desirable that money
should be expended in excess of or without the prior appropriation of
Parliament:
Provided that:
(i) the total amount of all sums issued and paid shall not exceed 1.5%
of the total amount of all sums appropriated by the Appropriation
Act or Acts for that year; and
(ii) in such case the Public Expenditure Review Committee shall
investigate and make a recommendation to the Minister of
Finance who may direct that any amount paid to any Government
Department or Crown Agency in accordance with paragraph (b)
be repaid to the Cook Islands Government Account out of any
appropriation in any following ﬁnancial year.
[Article 70: replaced, on 1 July 1997, by section 2 of the Constitution Amendment (No 22) Act 1997
(1997 No 17).]
Service 0116,501

71 Audit
(1) The Audit Of f ice of the Cook Islands shall be the auditor of the Cook Islands
Government Account and of all other public funds or accounts, and of the
accounts of all Departments and of f ices of executive government and of such
other public, statutory , or local authorities or bodies as may be provided by law .
(2) The Audit Of f ice shall, at least once annually , forward to the Speaker of
Parliament for presentation to Parliament a report containing such information
as is required to be submitted by any enactment, together with such other
information relating to the Cook Islands Government Account or other funds or
accounts which under this Constitution or under any other enactment are
required to be audited by the Audit Of f ice as that Of f ice considers desirable.
(3) There shall be established by enactment a Public Expenditure Review
Committee comprising a chairperson appointed by the Minister of Finance, and
other members whose number and manner of appointment shall be prescribed
by Act.
(4) The Act referred to in subclause (3) of this Article shall provide to the Public
Expenditure Review Committee suf f icient powers to investigate expenditure
from the Cook Islands Government Account and other public funds or accounts
of executive government and such other public statutory or local authorities or
bodies as may be prescribed by law , and shall have such other functions, duties,
powers, and responsibilities as shall be provided by enactment.
[Article 71(1): amended, on 12 August 1991, by section 4(1) of the Constitution Amendment (No
14) Act 1991 (1991 No 21).]
[Article 71(2): amended, on 5 June 1981, by section 6 and Schedule 2 of the Constitution
Amendment (No 9) Act 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Article 71(3): replaced, on 11 March 1996, by section 2 of the Constitution Amendment (No 18)
Act 1995–96 (1995–96 No 8).]
[Article 71(4): replaced, on 11 March 1996, by section 2 of the Constitution Amendment (No 18)
Act 1995–96 (1995–96 No 8).]

Part VI
The Cook Islands Public Service
[Part VI: replaced, on 1 July 1995, by section 8 of the Constitution Amendment (No 17) Act
1994–95 (1994–95 No 36).]
72 The Cook Islands Public Service
(1) There shall be a Cook Islands Public Service, which shall comprise such persons
in the service of the Government of the Cook Islands as may from time to time
be prescribed by law .
(2) An Act shall provide for the administration and regulations of the Cook Islands
Public Service including without limitation, the appointment, terms of service,
disciplinary control, termination of appointment, and dismissal of members of
the Public Service, and dif ferent such provisions may be made in respect of
dif ferent classes of members of the Public Service.
73 Public Service Commissioner
(1) There shall be a Public Service Commissioner appointed by the Queen’s
Representative on the advice of the Prime Minister.
(2) No person shall be appointed to be or remain the Public Service Commissioner
if he is or becomes a member of Parliament.
(3) The Public Service Commissioner shall not hold of f ice concurrently any other
of f ice in the Cook Islands Public Service.
(4) The actions of the Public Service Commissioner shall not be invalidated in
consequence of the subsequent discovery of some defect with regard to his
appointment.
(5) The Public Service Commissioner shall be paid such remuneration by way of
salary and allowances as may from time to time be determined by Cabinet.
(6) The procedure to be followed by the Public Service Commissioner in the
exercise of his functions, and the delegation of his powers and functions may be
prescribed by enactment.
74 T erm of of fice and functions of the Public Service Commissioner
(1) The Public Service Commissioner shall be appointed for such term as shall be
determined by Cabinet and may from time to time be reappointed.
(2) The Public Service Commissioner may at any time resign his of f ice by writing
under his hand addressed to the Prime Minister.
(3) The Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Prime Minister, may
suspend or remove the Public Service Commissioner from of f ice for disability ,
bankruptcy , neglect of duty , breach of the terms of his appointment, or
misconduct.
(4) The Public Service Commissioner shall have such functions as shall be
prescribed by Act.
75 Staf f of Queen’s Representative
(1) Except as provided in subclause (2) of this Article, the appointment, terms of
service, disciplinary control, termination of appointment, and dismissal of staf f
of the Queen’s Representative shall be matters for the Queen’s Representative,
acting in his discretion.
Service 0116,701

(2) The Queen’s Representative, if he so desires, may appoint to his staf f such
employees of the Cook Islands Public Service as he may select acting in his
discretion, but after consultation with the Prime Minister, from a list subjected
by the Public Service Commissioner; and the provisions of subclause (1) of this
Article (except so far as they relate to appointment) shall apply in relation to a
person so appointed in respect of his service on the staf f of the Queen’s
Representative but not in respect of his service as an employee of the Cook
Islands Public Service.
76 Board of Appeal
(1) There shall be a Cook Islands Public Service Board of Appeal, which shall
consist of—
(a) the Chief Justice of the High Court:
(b) one person, being an employee or former employee of the Cook Islands
Public Service, to be appointed by , and hold of f ice at the pleasure of, the
Queen’s Representative, acting on the advice of the Prime Minister:
(c) one person, being an employee or former employee of the Cook Islands
Public Service, to be elected by the employees of that Service or
nominated by an organisation of those employees, and to hold of f ice for
a period of 3 years.
(2) The Chief Justice shall be Chairman of the Board of Appeal.
(3) In the absence of the Chief Justice from any sitting of the Board of Appeal, any
other Judge of the High Court nominated by him either generally or in any
particular case, may attend the sitting in his stead, and while so attending shall
be Chairman of the Board of Appeal.
(4) In the absence of the Chief Justice or other Judge nominated pursuant to
subclause (3), the person for the time being holding of f ice as Ombudsman may
attend the sitting in his stead and while so acting shall be Chairman of the Board
of Appeal.
(5) An Act—
(a) shall prescribe whether or not the person to be appointed under the
provisions of paragraph (c) of subclause (1) of this Article is to be elected
or nominated and the manner of that election or nomination:
(b) may provide for the appointment of deputies to act for members of the
Board of Appeal appointed under the provisions of paragraph (b) or
paragraph (c) of subclause (1) of this Article:
(c) shall prescribe the jurisdiction of the Board of Appeal to hear and
determine appeals:
(d) shall prescribe the procedure of the Board of Appeal.
(6) Subject to the provisions of any Act, the Board of Appeal shall determine its
own procedure.
[The next page is 116,901]
Art 75LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 116,702

Part VIA
Miscellaneous provisions
[Part VIA: inserted, on 5 June 1981, by section 13 of the Constitution Amendment (No 9) Act
1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
76A Persons entitled to permanent residence
(1) A person has the status of a permanent resident of the Cook Islands if—
(a) the person is not entitled to the immigration status of a Cook Islander
under any Act; and
(b) the person is adopted by a person who is entitled to the immigration
status of a Cook Islander under any Act; and
(c) the person is adopted in a manner recognised by the laws of the Cook
Islands; and
(d) at the time of the adoption, the person is under 18 years; and
(e) the adoption is genuine and is not undertaken for the purpose of obtaining
permanent residence.
(1A) Subclause (1B) applies to a person—
(a) born before the commencement of the Constitution Amendment (No 29)
Act 2021 (the 2021 Amendment Act); and
(b) who was entitled to permanent residence under subclause (1) as it read
immediately before the commencement of the 2021 Amendment Act.
(1B) A person described in subclause (1A) continues to be entitled to permanent
residence.
(2) Any person may apply , pursuant to the provisions of an Act of Parliament, for
a certiﬁcate granting to him the status of a permanent resident of the Cook
Islands.
(3) An Act may—
(a) prescribe the qualiﬁcations to be held by a person to whom subclauses (2)
of this Article applies who is an applicant for such a certiﬁcate, and the
circumstances in which such an applicant is disqualiﬁed from being
granted such a certiﬁcate; and
(b) prescribe the conditions subject to which such a certiﬁcate may be
granted to a person to whom subclause (2) of this Article applies; and
(c) confer on a Minister a discretion to grant or refuse such a certiﬁcate to a
person to whom subclause (2) of this Article applies; and
(d) prescribe the circumstances in which such a certiﬁcate granted may be
revoked:
(e) prescribe the number of permanent residence certiﬁcates that may for the
time being, be in ef fect.
Provided that any certiﬁcate granted may only be revoked by a Judge of the
High Court.
(4) Notwithstanding any of the provisions of this Article, the Minister responsible
for immigration may cancel any certiﬁcate granted if the person to whom the
certiﬁcate relates is absent from the Cook Islands continuously for a period
exceeding 3 years in circumstances indicating that the person has ceased to
make his home in the Cook Islands.
Service 0116,901

(5) Nothing in this Article shall af fect the status as a permanent resident of the Cook
Islands of any person holding that status pursuant to the Entry , Residence, and
Departure Act 1971–72, immediately before the commencement of this Article.
[Article 76A(1): replaced, on 25 November 2021, by section 4 of the Constitution Amendment (No
29) Act 2021 (2021 No 8).]
[Article 76A(1A): inserted, on 25 November 2021, by section 4 of the Constitution Amendment (No
29) Act 2021 (2021 No 8).]
[Article 76A(1B): inserted, on 25 November 2021, by section 4 of the Constitution Amendment (No
29) Act 2021 (2021 No 8).]
[Article 76A(3)(e): inserted, on 12 December 1996, by section 2 of the Constitution Amendment
(No 19) Act 1995–96 (1995–96 No 33).]
76B The Prerogative of Mercy and Pardon
The Prerogative of Mercy and Pardon shall be exercised by the Queen’s
Representative, acting pursuant to a resolution of Parliament, provided that any
such resolution must receive the support of not less than two-thirds of the total
membership (including vacancies) of Parliament.
[Article 76B: amended, on 6 April 1982, by section 4(1) and Schedule of the Constitution
Amendment (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
76C The Cook Islands Ensign
(1) The Cook Islands Ensign shall be the ﬂag described in the Third Schedule to this
Constitution.
(2) The Cook Islands Ensign is hereby declared to be the recognised ﬂag of the
Cook Islands.
(3) Provision may be made by enactment prescribing the circumstances in which
and the conditions subject to which the Cook Islands Ensign may be ﬂown, and
prohibiting the defacing of the ensign by placing any sign, representation, or
letter thereon.
76D National Anthem of the Cook Islands
(1) The anthem entitled “T e Atua Mou E” shall be the national anthem of the Cook
Islands.
(2) The words of the national anthem shall be as set out in the Fourth Schedule to
this Constitution.
[The next page is 117,101]
Art 76ALA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 116,902

Part VII
T ransitional provisions
77 Existing law to continue
Subject to the provisions of this Constitution—
(a) the existing law shall, until repealed, and subject to any amendment
thereof, continue in force on and after Constitution Day:
(b) all rights, obligations, and liabilities arising under the existing law shall
continue to exist on and after Constitution Day , and shall be recognised,
exercised, and enforced accordingly .

81 Ordinances of Former Legislative Council or Legislative Assembly
(1) Every Ordinance made by the Legislative Council of the Cook Islands under
section 2 of the Cook Islands Amendment Act 1946, and in force immediately
before Constitution Day , shall be deemed to be an Ordinance of the Legislative
Assembly of the Cook Islands made before Constitution Day and shall continue
in force as if it were such an Ordinance on and after Constitution Day .
(2) All Ordinances made by the Legislative Assembly of the Cook Islands under
section 38 of the Cook Islands Amendment Act 1957, and in force immediately
before Constitution Day , shall continue in force on and after Constitution Day .
82 High Court
(1) The High Court of the Cook Islands established by Article 47 hereof is hereby
declared to be the same Court as the High Court of the Cook Islands established
by the Cook Islands Act 1915.
Service 0117,101

(2) The Judges and Commissioners of that Court in of f ice immediately before
Constitution Day shall continue to hold of f ice on and after Constitution Day as
if they had been appointed under the provisions of this Constitution, and those
Judges shall receive the salary to which they were entitled immediately before
Constitution Day as if that salary had been ﬁxed by enactment.
(3) All judgments, decrees, records, and acts of the High Court of the Cook Islands
shall continue to have full force and ef fect on and after Constitution Day as
judgments, decrees, records and acts of the High Court established under this
Constitution; and all proceedings, civil or criminal, pending in the High Court
immediately before Constitution Day , and all appeals pending immediately
before Constitution Day from decisions of the High Court, may be continued on
and after Constitution Day .
83 Land Court
(1) The Land Court of the Cook Islands established by Article 52 hereof is hereby
declared to be the same Court as the Native Land Court of the Cook Islands
established by the Cook Islands Act 1915.
(2) The Land Court of the Cook Islands shall also be deemed for all purposes to be
the same Court as that which existed at the commencement of the Cook Islands
Act 1915 under the name of the Cook Islands Land Titles Court, and all orders
theretofore made by the last-mentioned Court shall have ef fect accordingly .

T erm of of fice of His Excellency Apenera Short OBE

of f ice.

Representative during the period from 19 December 1993 to 11 October 1994
notwithstanding that His Excellency’s second term of of f ice did not begin until
11 October 1994 and will accordingly expire on 11 October 1997.

December 1993 to 11 October 1994 shall be as valid and ef fectual as if His
Excellency had been appointed as the Queen’s Representative by Her Majesty
the Queen during that period.

Second SchLA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 117,502

Third Schedule
Article 76C
The Cook Islands Ensign
[Third Schedule: inserted, on 5 June 1981, by section 16 and Schedule 3 of the Constitution Amendment (No
9) Act 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24). ]
The Cook Islands Ensign shall be described as follows:
The Cook Islands Ensign shall be a Royal blue ensign. The Union Jack shall occupy the upper staf f
quarter, having on the ﬂy 15 stars in a symmetrical ring, all of equal size and equal spacing, and the
colour of the stars shall be white. The ﬂag proportion of length to breath shall be two to one.
And it shall mean—
Blue — is the colour most expressive of our Nation, it is representative of the vast area
of the Paciﬁc Ocean in which the islands of the Cook Islands are scattered. Blue also
depicts the peaceful nature of the inhabitants of our islands.
Union Jack — indicates our historical association with and membership of the British
Commonwealth.
The 15 white stars — represent the 15 islands of the group.

Rarotonga e Pamati, e te Enua Mangaia, e te Enua Atiu

AKAMA T A ’ANGA
I ROTO I TE INGOA T APU O TE A TUA, TE TUT ARA, TE AROA AITEKORE E
TE MUTUKORE
Ko matou, te iti tangata o te Kuki Airani, tei irinaki i te au apii’anga Keresitiano, te peu
enua o te Kuki Airani, e te ture, te akama’ara i te Sabati e ra T apu, koia oki te ra o te
epetoma tei irinaki tetai uatu e, ko te Sabati no te Atua.
[Upoko roa: tauru’ia, i te ra 19 March 1997, e te tuanga 2; Akatuke’anga Papa Ture metua (No 20) Act 1997
(1997 No 2).]
1 Aite’anga
(1) I roto i teia Papa Ture Metua, ma ¯ri ua me anoano ia te aite’anga,—
T ure nuikoia oki ko tetai ture a te Paramani o te Kuki Airani
Ka ¯ pinetikoia oki ko te Ka ¯pineti o te au Minita o te Kuki Airani
Papa T ure Metuakoia oki ko teia Papa Ture Metua; e pera te au akatuke’anga
ki te reira
Ra ¯ Akama’ara Uti’anga Reva koia oki ko te ra ¯ i akataka ia no te akamata’anga
o teia Papa Ture Metua
T e Kuki Airani koia oki ko te au enua katoa i roto i te Moana T onga o te
Patipika e vai ra i rotopu i te 8 e te 23 tikirı ¯ti o te tua tonga e pera 156 e te 157
tikirı ¯ti i te tua roa opunga o te Greenwich; e te au enua tatakitai o te Kuki Airani
koia te au enua rikiriki e noo ra 10 maire te mamao mei te tapa taatai
Akava’anga Apı ¯ra koia oki ko te Akava’anga Apı ¯ra o te Kuki Airani tei
akatupu ia i raro ake i teia Papa Ture Metua
T angata angaanga no te Korona koia ko tetai uatu tangata angaanga a te
Korona, me kore tareketa, mema me kore, tangata angaanga no tetai tuanga a te
Korona me kore, tetai uatu kopapa me kore, taokotai’anga i raro ake i te tamaru
anga me kore, akatere anga a te Korona me kore, e mema o te Konitara Enua,
inara kare te mema Paramani me kore Minita
akamana’anga koia oki ko tetai Ture nui a te Paramani o te Kuki Airani, Ture
akatere enua, tetai uatu ture nui a te Paramani o Nu Tireni e ta’angaanga ia nei
i te Kuki Airani, e tetai uatu Akakite’anga, akaue’anga, tureiti, me kore tetai ture
enua a te Konitara Enua
Konitara Aka’aere koia oki ko te Konitara Aka’aere o te Kuki Airani tei
akatupu ia i raro ake i teia Papa Ture Metua
ture ta’angaanga koia oki ko tetai uatu ture e ta’angaanga ia nei i roto i te Kuki
Airani i mua ake i te ra Akama’ara’anga Uti anga Reva; e pera te au ture i ariiki
ia e tei maani ia i mua ake i te Ra Uti’anga reva e tei akamana ia e te
ta’angaanga ia i muri ake i te Ra Uti’anga Reva
Komitiona T eitei[T akore’ia]
Akava’anga T eitei koia oki ko te Akava’anga T eitei o te Kuki Airani tei
akatupu ia i raro ake i teia Papa Ture Metua
Opita o te Akava’anga koia oki ko te Akava nui Maata me kore, Akava nui no
te Akava’anga Apı ¯ra me kore, Akava’anga T eitei, me kore Akava no te ‘Au e
rave ra i te angaanga akava’anga
Akava’anga Apı ¯ra Enua [T akore’ia]
Service 0122,201

Akava’anga Enua [T akore’ia]
T urekoia ko tetai uatu ture e ta’angaanga ia ra i te Kuki Airani; kapiti atu teia
Papa Ture Metua e tetai atu au ture i akamana ia
Are Maani T uretei akataka ia i roto i teia Papa Ture Metua me kore, tetai uatu
ture i akamana ia e te Paramani o te Kuki Airani i raro ake i teia Papa Ture
Metua
Minita koia ko tetai Minita o te Kavamani o te Kuki Airani; kapiti katoa mai te
Parai Minita
Nu Tireni koia oki ko Nu Tireni i vao ake i te Kuki Airani
T ure Akatere Enuakoia oki ko tetai Ture a te Are Maani Ture o te Kuki Airani
tei maani ia i mua ake i te Ra Uti’anga Reva e te mana ra i mua ake e, i muri
ake i te Ra Uti’anga Reva
Paramani koia oki ko te Paramani o te Kuki Airani tei akatupu ia i raro ake i
teia Papa Ture Metua, e ko te tuatua “Are Maani Ture” me kore “Maani Ture”
tei a ¯ta mai i roto i teia Papa Ture Metua me kore, tetai uatu ture kua aiteite rai
te aite’anga
Peremia [T akore’ia]
Parai Minita me koia ko te Parai Minita o te Kuki Airani
Kauono o te Ariki V ainekoia oki ko te kauono o T ona Ngateitei te Ariki V aine
i te Kuki Airani tei iki’ia i raro ake i te Atikara 3 i mua akenei.
kia noo [T akore’ia]
(2) I raro ake i te au akataka’anga o teia Papa Ture Metua ka anoano ia tetai uatu
tangata kia rave i tetai taputou anga tana i tia e ka rauka iaia i te rave e te a ¯ru
katoa i te reira na roto i tana i papa’u.
(3) I roto i teia Papa Ture Metua kua akaa ¯ri mai te reira i te au angaanga a tetai opati
e pera te au mana e te tika’anga o te au tangata angaanga ka rave ki roto i reira.
[Atikara 1(1) Ture nui: akatuke’ia, i te ra 5 o Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(1) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) Akava’anga Apı ¯ra: tauru iatu, I te ra 5 o Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(2) Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) T angata angaanga no te Korona: tauru iatu, i te ra 1 Tiurai 1995, e te tuanga 2(a) o te
Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 17) Ture nui 1994–95 (1994–95 No 36).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) akamana’ia: akatuke ia, i te ra 5 June 1981, e te tuanga 2(1) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Act 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) Komitiona T eitei: takore ia, i te ra 6 April 1982, e te tuanga 4(2(a) o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Act 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) opita o te ture: tauru iatu, i te ra 1 Tiurai 1995, e te tuanga 2(b) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 17) Act 1994–95 (1994–95 No 36).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) Akava’anga Akarakara no te Enua: takore’ia, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(3) o
te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[A¯tikara 1(1) Akava’anga Enua: takore’ia, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(3) o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Act 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 1(1) Are Maani Ture me kore Amani Ture: mono ia, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(3)
o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 1(1) Minita: mono ia, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(4) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Act 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 1(1) Paramani: tauru iatu, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(5) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 1(1) Peremia: takore ia, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(6) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 1(1) Parai Minita: tauru iatu, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 2(6) o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 1(1) Kauono o te Ariki V aine: itauru iatu, I te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(2)(b) o te
Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 1(1) kia noo: takore ia, i te ra 10 T epetema 2003, e te tuanga 2 o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 26) Ture nui 2003 (2003 No 15).]
Atikara 1LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 122,202

Pae I
T e Kavamani o te Kuki Airani
2 T e Upoko o te Basileia
Ko T ona Ngateitei te Ariki V aine na roto i te tika’anga o Nu Tireni te Upoko
T a ¯maru o te Kuki Airani.
T e Kauono o te Ariki V aine
[Akaupoko: mono ia, I te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 2 o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
3 T e Kauono o te Ariki V aine i te Kuki AIrani
(1) E kauono to T ona Ngateitei te Ariki V aine ka iki ia i te Kuki Airani, ka kapiki
ia e ko te Kauono o te Ariki V aine.
(2) Ko te Kauono o te Ariki V aine ka iki ia te reira e T ona Ngateitei te Ariki V aine,
e ka tiaki aia i te reira opati no tetai 3 mataiti, e ka iki akaou ia aia mei tetai
taime ki tetai.
[Atikara 3: mono ia, i te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 2 o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
4 T aputou’anga
I mua ake ka akamata ei te Kauono o te Ariki V aine i te rave i te au angaanga
no teia opati, ka oronga atu aia ki mua i te Akava nui T eitei o te Akava’anga
T eitei i teia taputou anga—
Koau ko, . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .,
T e taputou nei au ki te Atua Mana e ka tavini au ma te tiratiratu ¯ e te tau tikai i
T ona Ngateitei te Ariki V aine [me kore Ariki T ane] [Akataka i te ingoa o te
Ariki mei te: Ariki V aine Elizabeth Rua] te Upoko T a ¯maru o te Basileia Kuki
Airani, tana anau e te ka mono mai iaia, kia tau ki te ture, e ka tiaki au ma te
tau tikai i te opati o te Kauono o te Ariki V aine ma te rave i te au angaanga
meitaki no te Kuki Airani kia tau i raro ake i te Papa Ture Metua e te ture. Ko
te Atua toku tauturu.
[Atikara 4: akatuke ia, i te ra 1 Okotopa 1975, e te tuanga 2(a) e te tuanga 2 o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 7) Ture nui 1975 (1975 No 17); i te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e te
Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
5 T e Kauono o te Ariki V aine kia rave i tei akaue ia
(1) Ma te kore e akataka anga ke ¯ mei tei akakite ia i roto i teia Papa Ture Metua nei,
i roto i tana rave anga i te au angaanga Kauono no te Ariki V aine, ka rave aia i
te angaanga ka akaue ia aia e te Ka ¯pineti, te Parai Minita me kore, te Minita tau,
kia tau ki te akakoro’anga.
(2) Mei te mea e tuku atu te Ka ¯pineti, Parai Minita, me kore tetai Minita i tetai
akaue anga ki te Kauono o te Ariki V aine no tetai o te au angaanga i anoano ia
aia kia rave, e mei te mea e kare te Kauono o te Ariki V aine e rave i te reira i
roto i te 14 au ra i muri ake i te tuku anga iatu teia akaue anga kiaia kia rave mei
tei akataka ia e teia Papa Ture Metua me kore, tetai uatu ture, ko te aite’anga i
reira kua ariki aia i te reira akaue anga; ka tuku atu i reira te T ekeretere o te
Service 0122,203

Ka ¯pineti i tetai akakite anga i raro ake i te akaue anga a te Parai Minita e kia
rave ia te angaanga i akakoro ia mei tei akaue ia kiaia.
[Atikara 5 upoko: akatuke ia, i te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e te Akapapa’anga o te Papa
Ture Metua (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 5(1): akatuke ia, i te ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 3(3) e te Akapapa’anga 1 Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24); i te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1)
e te Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture Metua (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 5(2): akatuke ia, on 5 June 1981, e te tuanga 3(3) e te Akapapa’anga 1 o te Papa ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24); i te ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1)
e te Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No
20).]
6 Karere ki te Kauono o te Ariki V aine
Ka riro e na te Parai Minita—
(a) e akateateamamao i te kave anga o te au tumu manako e te au meneti
uipa’anga a te Ka ¯pineti e tetai atu au peapa tei uriuri ia e te Ka ¯pineti ki
te Kauono o te Ariki V aine i te tuatau e tu’a iatu ei te reira ki te au Minita;
e pera
(b) te tuku anga atu i te au karere no runga i te au angaanga o te Kuki Airani
e te au tamanako anga no te ture ta te Kauono o te Ariki V aine ka kapiki.
[Atikara 6 upoko: akatuke ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e pera te Akakapapa’anga o te Papa
Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 6: akatuke ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 3(3) e pera te Akakapapa’anga o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 6(a): akatuke ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e pera te Akakapapa’anga o te Papa
Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20)]
[Atikara 6(b): akatuke ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e pera te Akakapapa’anga o te Papa
Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
7 T auturu Kauono o te Ariki V aine
(1) I te tuatau e kua va ¯ te opati o te Kauono o te Ariki V aine me kore, kua a ¯tea atu
te Kauono o te Ariki V aine ki vao ake i te Kuki Airani me kore, no tetai uatu
tumu anga e kare e rauka i te rave i te au angaanga i akataka ia e te ture kia rave
aia, ka riro te reira au angaanga e na te Akavanui T eitei o te Kuki Airani, me
kore, me kare e rauka i te Akavanui T eitei i te rave i te reira au angaanga no tetai
au tumu anga ke ¯, ka riro e na te Akavanui o te Akava’anga T eitei tei akamana
ia e te Atikara 50 o teia Papa Ture e rave i te reira tei akataka mai i te au
angaanga a te Akavananui T eitei.
(2) Kare e ngai i roto i teia Atikara e arai i te Kauono o te Ariki V aine mei te rave
i te au angaanga i akataka ia aia kia rave e te ture i tetai uatu taime mei te mea
e kua a ¯tea atu aia mei te Kuki Airani.
(3) Ko te au angaanga i rave ia e te Akavanui T eitei o te Kuki Airani me kore,
Akavanui o te Akava’anga T eitei no te turanga o te Akavanui T eitei no te rave
anga i te au angaanga i akataka ia na te Kauono o te Ariki V aine, kare te reira
e ui ia me kore, takore ia mei te mea e, kare te akakoro’anga i tupu me kore kua
akakore ia te reira.
[Atikara 7: mono ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 3 Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture
nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
T e Are Ariki o te Kuki Airani
8 T e Are Ariki o te Kuki Airani
(1) Ka akatupu ia tetai Are Ariki no te Kuki Airani (ko te ka kapiki ia e ko te Are
Ariki).
Atikara 5LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 0 122,204

(2) Ko teia te au mema o te Are Ariki:
(a) te au Ariki e 4 no te enua Aitutaki e Manuae:
(b) te au Ariki e 3 no te enua Atiu:
(c) te Ariki no te enua Mangaia:
(d) te Ariki no te enua Manihiki:
(e) te Ariki no te enua Rakahanga:
(f) te au Ariki e 3 no te enua Mauke:
(g) te au Ariki e 3 no te enua Mitiaro:
(h) te Ariki no te enua Penrhyn:
(i) te Ariki no nga enua Pukapuka e Nassau:
(j) te au Ariki e 6 no te enua Rarotonga.
(3) Kia tau ki te au akataka anga o teia Atikara, no te au mema o te Are Ariki, ka
akamana ia ratou e te Kauono o te Ariki V aine.
(4) [ T akore’ia]
(5) [ T akore’ia]
(6) Kia tau ki te au akataka anga o teia Atikara, no runga i te au tika’anga o te au
Ariki, tei tau me kore, kare e tau ei au mema no te Are Ariki, pera te au
akanoo’noo anga e te au turanga no to ratou riro anga ei au mema kua akataka
ia te reira e te ture.
(7) Mei te mea e va ¯ tetai ngai o tetai mema i roto i te Are Ariki, ka mono iatu te reira
mei tei rave ia ki te iki’anga o te mema i akangaroi, e ka mou te mema o ¯ u i te
taonga no te tuatau toe o te reira mema.
[Atikara 8(2): mono ia, ra 5 Noema 2002, e te tuanga 2(a) o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
25) Ture nui 2002 (2002 No 8).]
[Atikara 8(3): akatuke’ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) epera te Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke’anga(No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 8(4): takore’ia, ra 5 Noema 2002, e te tuanga 2(b) o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
25) Ture nui 2002 (2002 No 8).]
[Atikara 8(5): takore’ia, ra 5 Noema 2002, e te tuanga 2(b) o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
25) Ture nui 2002 (2002 No 8).]
9 Au Angaanga a te Are Ariki
T eia te au angaanga a te Are Ariki i raro nei:
(a) ko te akara i te au manako puapinga ka riro ei meitaki no te iti tangata o
te Kuki Airani ta te Paramani ka tuku atu kia uriuri ia, e kia akaoki katoa
atu i to ratou manako e te au tamanako anga katoa ki te Paramani;
(b) te rave atu i tetai au angaanga ke ¯ tei akataka ia e te ture.
[Atikara 9(a): akatuke’ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 6 e te Akapapa’anga 2 o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
10 Au Mema kia T aputou
T akake ¯ mei te anoano o teia Atikara, kare tetai mema o te Are Ariki e tika ia kia
piri atu me kore, iki atu ma ¯ri ua kua rave aia i te taputou anga ki mua i te aroaro
o te Kauono o te Ariki V aine koia oki:
Koau ko, . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .,
T e taputou nei au ki te Atua Mana e ka tavini au ma te tiratiratu ¯ e te tau tikai i T ona
Ngateitei te Ariki V aine [me kore Ariki T ane] [Akataka i te ingoa o te Ariki mei te:
Ariki V aine Elizabeth Rua] te Upoko T a ¯maru o te Basileia Kuki Airani, tana anau
e te ka mono mai iaia, kia tau ki te ture, e ka rave au i te au angaanga tau tei
anoano ia ei mema no te Are Ariki o te Kuki Airani. Ko te Atua toku tauturu.

Service 0122,205

[Atikara 10: akatuke’ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e pera te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga
(No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
11 T omo’anga mai te Parai Minita e tetai au tangata takake ki roto i te Are
Ariki
(1) Ka tomo mai te Parai Minita i tetai uatu tuatau e pera tuatua mai ki te Are Ariki.
(2) Ko tetai Minita me kore, tangata tei iki ia e te Minita ei kaouno nona, ka tika ia
kia piri atu ki te au uipaanga a te Are Ariki mei te mea e ko tetai au manako e
uriuri ia ra e te Are Ariki tei raro ake i tana akatere anga.
(3) Mei te mea e kua irinaki te tama akatere o te Are Ariki e ko tetai tumu manako
i mua i te Are Ariki e kua tau kia pati iatu tetai uatu mema Paramani kia tomo
mai ki roto i te uipaanga a te Are Ariki no te piri’anga ki te reira tumu manako.
(4) Ko tetai tangata ka piri atu ki roto i te uipaanga a te Are Ariki kia tau i raro ake
i te au akataka’anga o te irava-iti (2) me kore (3) o teia Atikara, ka tika ia aia kia
piri atu ki roto i te uriuri anga manako a te Are no te pirianga ki te reira tuanga
i raro ake i te akatere anga a tona Minita i pati ia, mei te mea atura aia e, e mema
aia no te Are Ariki.
Inara, kare aia e tika ia i te iki i roto i te Are Ariki me kore, i roto i tona au
kumiti.
[Atikara 11 upoko: akatuke’ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 3(3) e te Akapapa’anga 1 o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 11(1): akatuke’ia, ra 5 June 1981, e te tuanga 3(3)) e te Akapapa’anga 1 o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
[Atikara 11(3): akatuke’ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 6 e te Akapapa’anga 2 o te Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24).]
11A Akanoo’noo anga
(1) Ka akatere iatu te uipaanga a te Are Ariki e tetai o tona mema, ka iki ia e te au
mema o te Are Ariki na roto i te akanoo’noo anga tei akataka ia e te ture e ka
mou ratou i te taonga no te tuatau e te turanga tei akataka ia e te ture.
(2) Ka uipa te Are Ariki ki Rarotonga i te au tuatau i akataka ia e te ture:
Ka uipa te Are Ariki mei te okotai taime i roto i te 12 marama.
(3) Ka kapiki ia te au uipaanga a te Are Ariki e te Kauono o te Ariki V aine, kia tau
ki te akaue anga a te Parai Minita.
(4) Kare e rave ia te uipaanga a te Are Ariki mei te mea e tei raro ake te numero
mema i te 8.
(5) Kia tau ki te au akataka’anga o teia Papa Ture Metua e te au akataka’anga o tetai
uatu ture, ka rauka i te Are Ariki mei tetai taime ki tetai i te maani, akatuke e
pera takore i te au Akatere’anga Uipaanga no te ture iti e te akatano anga i te
turanga uipaanga e te au atuitui anga karere.
(6) Kia tau ki te au akataka’anga o teia Atikara e tetai au akataka’anga o tetai uatu
ture, na te Are Ariki rai e akanoo i tana au rave’anga angaanga.
(7) Kare te Are Ariki e aka’apa ia no te rave’anga o tetai angaanga noatu e ngai va ¯
tetai i roto i tona au mema, e ko te au uriuri anga manako kua tau te reira noatu
oki e, ko tetai au tangata kare o ratou tika anga me kore i te iki i roto i te Are
me kore piri ki roto i te au uipaanga.
[Atikara 11A(3): akatuke’ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 3(3) e pera Akapapa’anga 1 o te PapaTure
Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24); ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1)
e te Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No
20).]

Service 0 122,206

11B Au Tika’anga o te Are Ariki e tona au mema
Ka maani ia tetai au akataka’anga e te ture no te piri’anga o te Are Ariki e tona
au mema e pera, au opita, te au tangata ka tika ia i te tuatua, e te au tangata ta ¯ta ¯
tuatua i raro ake i te tika a te Are no tetai ripoti, peapa, iki’anga me kore au
angaanga tei akataka ia i raro ake i tetai uatu ture tei akamana ia no runga i te
au tika’anga e te paruru anga a te Paramani, no tona au mema e te au opita, e
pera te au tangata akakitekite karere tei tamaru ia e te tika’anga a te Paramani.
[Atikara 11B: akatuke’ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 6 e te Akapapa’anga 2 Papa Ture Metua
Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980– 81 (1980–81 No 24).]

Pae II
T e Konitara Aka’aere o te Kavamani Kuki Airani
12 Mana Akatere
(1) Ko te mana akatere o te Kuki Airani kua tango ia i roto T ona Ngateitei T e Ariki
V aine na roto ia Nu Tireni.
(2) Kia tau ki te au akataka anga o teia Papa Ture Metua, ko te mana akatere o te
Kuki Airani ka ta’angaanga ia no T ona Ngateitei e te Kauono o te Ariki V aine
mei iaia me kore na roto i tona au tangata angaanga i raro ake iaia.
(3) Kare tetai tuanga i roto i teia Atikara e riro i te paruru atu i te Paramani mei te
uriuri i te au angaanga a te au tangata me kore akatere anga mei te Kauono o te
Ariki V aine.
[Atikara 12(2): akatuke’ia, ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e t Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture
Metua Akatuke ’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 12(3): akatuke’ia, ra 5 Tiunu 1981, e te tuanga 6 e pera Apapa’anga 2 o te Turenui 1980–81
(1980–81 No 24); ra 6 Aperira 1982, e te tuanga 4(1) e te (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82 (1981–82 No
20).]
Ka ¯ pineti
13 Ka ¯ pineti
(1) Ka iki ia tetai Ka ¯pineti no te au Minita, koia oki ko te Parai Minita o te Kuki
Airani (nana e akatere i te Ka ¯pineti) e te au minita kare i runga ake i te 6 au
Minita, ko ratou te au tangata akaaere e te arataki i te kavamani akatere o te
Kuki Airani e te ripoti anga ki te Paramani.
(2) Au takainga no te iki anga i te Parai Minita:
(a) Mei te mea e rave ia te iki anga i te tuatau e uipa ra te Paramani, ka iki
te Kauono o te Ariki V aine i tetia mema Paramani e arataki ra i te maata
anga o te au mema Paramani.
(b) Mei te mea e rave ia te iki anga i te tuatau e kare te Paramani e uipa ana,
ka iki atu te Kauono o te Ariki V aine ei Parai Minita tetai mema Paramani
tana i irinaki e tei iaia te maata anga o te au mema Paramani.
(c) Mei te mea e rave ia te iki anga i muri ake i te takore anga ia te Paramani
e i mua ake i te iki’anga maata no te Paramani i muri ake i te takore anga
Paramani, ka iki viviki atu te Kauono o te Ariki V aine ei Parai Minita i
tetai tangata tei mema Paramani mai ana i mua ake ite takore anga e tana
i irinaki e tei iaia te maata anga o te au mema Paramani i mua ake i te
takore anga o te Paramani:
Kia tau rai oki ki tei akataka ia, ko te takore anga o te Paramani kua rave
ia i raro ake i te tuangaiti (2) o te Atikara 37, ka iki viviki atu i reira te
Kauono o te ariki V aine ei Parai Minita i tetai mema Paramani i mua ake
i te takore anga Paramani tana i irinaki e ka rauka I te rave i te au
angaanga a te Parai Minita.
(3) E rima au Minita, takake mei te Parai Minita, ka iki ia e te Kauono o te Ariki
V aine i raro ake i te akaue anga a te Parai Minita. Kare e tangata e iki ia i raro
ake i teia tuangaiti ma ¯ri ua—
(a) e mema Paramani te reira tangata; me kore
(b) mei te mea e ko te iki anga ka rave ia i muri ake i te takore anga o te
Service 1122,401

Paramani e, i mua ake i te iki’anga maata i muri ake i te takore anga, e
ko te reira tangata e mema Paramani aia i mua ake i te takore anga o te
Paramani; me kore
(c) mei te mea kua rave ia te iki anga i muri ake i te iki anga maata no te
Paramani e i mua ake i te akamata anga o te uipaanga mua a te Paramani
I muri ake i te reria iki anga maata, kua riro te iki anga o te reira tangata
tangata i te akapapu iaia ei mema Paramani i roto i taua iki anga maata.
(3A) Okotai Minita takake ¯ mei te Parai Minita, tei iki ia e te Parai Minita, ka akamana
ia e te Kauono o te Ariki V aine kia tau ki tei akakite ia e te Parai Minita mei te
au tangata i akataka ia i roto i te paraka ¯va (a), (b) o te iravaiti (3) e ko tei—
(a) be qualiﬁed for election as a member of Parliament on and for the
duration of his appointment; andtau kia iki ia ei mema Paramani no te
tuatau o tona iki anga ia; e pera
(b) ka tika ia kia tomo e pera, tuatua i roto i te au uipaanga a te Paramani e
tetai uatu kumiti o reira mei te mea atura e mema Paramani tikai aia inara,
kare aia e tika ia i te iki ki runga i tetai uatu ui’anga i mua i te Paramanai.
(4) Ko te au iki anga i raro ake i te au akataka anga o teia Atikara ka oronga ia na
roto i te peapa akamana anga i raro ake i te T apao anga o te Kuki Airani.
(5) Mei te mea tetai tangata angaanga a te Kavamani Kuki Airani e iki ia ei Minita,
ka karanga ia i reira e kua akaa ¯tea aia mei tona opati angaanga.
[Atikara 13(1): mono ia, ra 12 Ma ¯ti 1999, e te tuanga 2(a) o te Papa ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
23) Ture nui 1999 (1999 No 4).]
[Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 9) Ture nui 1980–81 (1980–81 No 24); ra 6 Aperira 1982, e
te tuanga 4(1) e te Akapapa’anga o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 10) Ture nui 1981–82
(1981–82 No 20).]
[Atikara 13(3): mono ia, ra 12 Ma ¯ti 1999, e te tuanga 2(a) Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No 23)
Ture nui 1999 (1999 No 4).]
[Atikara 13(3A): tauru ia, ra 12 Ma ¯ti 1999, e te tuanga 2(b) o te Papa ture Metua Akatuke’anga (No
23) Ture nui 1999 (1999 No 4).]
14 T uatau mou taonga o te au mema o te Ka ¯ pineti
(1) Ko te iki anga o te Parai Minita e mou ra i te taonga tei rave ia i mua ake i te
ra tei akataka ia no te iki anga maata no te Paramani, ka takore ia te reira e te
Kauono o te Ariki V aine i muri ake i te ra o te reira iki anga e pera, i mua ake
i te uipaanga mua a te Paramanai i muri ake i te oti anga o te iki anga maata.
(2) [ T akore’ia]
(3) Ko te iki anga katoa o te Parai Minita ka takore katoa ia e te Kauono o te Ariki
V aine—
(a) mei te mea e akaoti te Parai Minita mei te mema Paramani no tetai tumu
anga ke ¯ takake mei te takore anga o te Paramani; me kore
(b) mei te mea e kua pa ¯ti te Paramani i tetai akakeu’anga i te akakite i te
irinaki kore ki roto i te Ka ¯pineti me kore kua ru ¯ ti tetai akakeu’anga me
kore manamanata ta te Parai Minita i akakite e, kare e irinaki anga:
Ma ¯ri ua, mei te mea i muri ake i te pa ¯ti anga te akakeu’anga, me kore i
muri ake i te patianga a te Parai Minita no tei kore i manuia, ka takore atu
te Kauono o te Ariki V aine i te Paramani na roto i tona mana e kare e
takore i te iki anga o te Parai Minita; me kore
(c) mei te mea e akaoti te Parai Minita mei tona taonga na roto i te ta ¯ta ¯’anga
peapa ki te Kauono o te Ariki V aine; me kore
Atikara 13LA WS OF THE COOK ISLANDS
Service 1 122,402

(d) mei te mea e kare te Parai minita i roto nei i te Kuki Airani no tetai
akakoro’anga ke ¯ atu e kare e no te kavamani no tetai tuatau tere atu i te
3 marama ma te kore e akatika anga ta ¯ta ¯ mei ko mai i te Kauono o te
Ariki V aine
(4) Ko te taonga o tetai o te au Minita ka va ¯ te reira—
(a) mei te mea e kua takore ia te taoanga o te Parai Minita i raro ake i te
iravaiti (1) me kore (3) o teia Atikara; me kore
(b) mei te mea te taonga o te Minita e kua takore ia e te Kauono o te Ariki
V aine mei tei akaue ia e te Parai Minita na roto i te ta ¯ta ¯’anga i raro ake
i te T apao o te Kuki Airani; me kore
(c) mei te mea te Minita, e mema no te Paramani, e akaoti mei te mema
Paramani no tetai tumu anga ke ¯ takake mei te takore anga o te Paramani;
me kore
(d) mei te mea te Minita, e kare i te mema Paramani, kare e tika’anga akaou
kia iki ia ei mema Paramani; me kore
(e) mei te mea e akaoti te Minita mei tona taonga na roto i te ta ¯ta ¯ atu anga
ki te Kauono o te Ariki V aine.
(5) Ma ¯ri ua, no te akakoro’anga maki me kore, kare te Parai Minita i te Kuki Airani
nei no tetai tuatau poto kare i rauka i te rave ia tana angaanga, ka iki atu te
Kauono o te Ariki V aine na roto i te ta ¯ta ¯ anga i raro ake i te T apao o te Kuki
Airani i tetai Minita kia rave i tana au angaanga e tae rava atu ki te tuatau e
rauka akaou ei i te Parai Minita i te rave i te reira me kore, kua akaoti i te
angaanga.
(6) Ko te mana tei oronga ia ki te Kauono o te Ariki V aine i raro ake i te au
akataka’anga o te iravaiti (5) o teia Atikara, ka ta’angaanga te Kauono o te Ariki
V aine i te reira, mei te mea kua irinaki aia e kare e anoano ia te akakite anga mei
ko mai i te Parai Minita no te mea e maki me kore kua a ¯tea atu aia ki vao ake
i te enua e, me no tetai uatu tumu anga, ka ta’angaanga te Kauono o te Ariki
V aine i tona mana kia tau ki te akaue anga mei ko mai i te Parai Minita.
(7) I te Kauono o te Ariki V aine, ka rave i te angaanga i akaue ia mai e te Parai
Minita na roto i te ta ¯ta ¯ anga i raro ake i te Akairo T aputou o te Kuki Airani—
(a) Akapapu ¯ mai no tetai Minita e kua maki ia no tetai tuatau poto e kare e
rauka i te rave i tana angaanga Minita; me kore
(b) kopae i tetai Minita i te tuatau e rave ia ra tetai kimikimi anga ki roto i
tona turanga Minita.
(8) Ko tetai Minita tei rave ia tetai angaanga kia tau i raro ake i te au akataka’anga
o te iravaiti (7) o teia Atikara, kare aia e rave i te au angaanga no tona opati me
kore noo ki reira me kore kare e piri atu ki roto i te au uipaanga a te Ka ¯pineti
me kore Konitara Akatere mari ua, kia takore rava ia tona au arai anga e te
Kauono o te Ariki V aine na roto i te ta ¯ta ¯’anga i raro ake i te T apao anga o te
Kuki Airani kia tau oki ki te akakite anga a te Parai Minita.
[Atikara 14(1): mono ia, ra 30 Noema 1993, e te tuanga 2(a) o te Papa Ture Metua Akatuke’anga
(No 15) Ture nui 1993 (1993 No 10).]
